  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_15d35fe5-f1e7-406d-b3b8-df57f7fe9d33'
      });

Lily realizes she’s kind of falling for this letter writer. Only, who is he? <div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/55570388-fairytalesbliss"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1506778540i/55570388._UY100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/55570388-fairytalesbliss">Fairytalesbliss</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Kasie West has answered this question:<br /><br />“Unfortunately books can't continue indefinitely, right? Lily and Cade do continue on after the story, though. I<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Kasie West has answered this question:<br /><br />“Unfortunately books can't continue indefinitely, right? Lily and Cade do continue on after the story, though. I'm not sure if she wins the contest. I thought about that question while I was writing the book and was going to answer it in the book but then I realized it wasn't about if she won the contest or not. It was about how she found the courage to submit her writing and have other people read it. That is a lifelong win for her. Winning the contest would've just been a one time thing, winning confidence will allow her to ultimately win in life because she'll try more things and put herself out there creatively more.”<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

I Like You</span></div><div class="reviewCta__controls" data-reactid=".275up9q15hc.1.1"><div class="userRating" data-reactid=".275up9q15hc.1.1.0"><div class="userRating__starsWrapper" tabindex="0" role="group" data-reactid=".275up9q15hc.1.1.0.1"><button class="userRating__star userRating__star--mediumStars" title="Rate 1 star" data-reactid=".275up9q15hc.1.1.0.1.$1"></button><button class="userRating__star userRating__star--mediumStars" title="Rate 2 stars" data-reactid=".275up9q15hc.1.1.0.1.$2"></button><button class="userRating__star userRating__star--mediumStars" title="Rate 3 stars" data-reactid=".275up9q15hc.1.1.0.1.$3"></button><button class="userRating__star userRating__star--mediumStars" title="Rate 4 stars" data-reactid=".275up9q15hc.1.1.0.1.$4"></button><button class="userRating__star userRating__star--mediumStars" title="Rate 5 stars" data-reactid=".275up9q15hc.1.1.0.1.$5"></button></div></div><button class="gr-button u-marginTopBottomXSmall reviewCta__writeButton" data-reactid=".275up9q15hc.1.1.1">Write a review</button></div></div></div></div>

<div id="review_1715122658" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1715122658" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1715122658?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-drama">teen-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-hate-relationships">love-hate-relationships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1715122658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14557792666476747984">Believe me, I’m even more shocked and distraught than you are.<br/><br/>I like Kasie West. Her stories, although always somewhat clichéd, are charming and, quite frankly, I never thought I would one day feel completely indifferent about one of her books.<br/><br/>Well, we do need to make something clear first: <strong>this isn’t bad</strong>. In fact, it can be sweet and adorable at times.<br/><br/>But it’s so full of high school tropes. They’re everywhere and all the time. Ubiquitous, truly.<br/><br/>Boy drama? Check. Boy-related misunderstandings? C</span>
  <span id="freeText14557792666476747984" style="display:none">Believe me, I’m even more shocked and distraught than you are.<br /><br />I like Kasie West. Her stories, although always somewhat clichéd, are charming and, quite frankly, I never thought I would one day feel completely indifferent about one of her books.<br /><br />Well, we do need to make something clear first: <strong>this isn’t bad</strong>. In fact, it can be sweet and adorable at times.<br /><br />But it’s so full of high school tropes. They’re everywhere and all the time. Ubiquitous, truly.<br /><br />Boy drama? Check. Boy-related misunderstandings? Check. Girl torn over two boys, arguably three? Check. Miss bitchy popular gal trying to ruin the heroine’s love life? Check. Boy-related best friend drama? Check.<br /><br />And it goes on and on and on.<br /><br />I guess you could say that I am not the right person to be reading this book. If I hadn’t read hundreds and hundreds of YA novels with similar themes, I may have given this a three-star rating. But not more.<br /><br />Because although it’s fast-paced and charming at times, it never really is <em>original. </em>It’s very clichéd, and normally I don’t mind it that much from Kasie West, since her humour usually manages to reduce my dislike of the clichéd parts, but this time it just didn’t work.<br /><br />Maybe my reaction to <em>P.S. I Like You </em>would have been different if Cade had been more loveable and it hadn’t taken me 3/4 of the story to finally consider him a sweetheart. His bad boy act – from the point of view of Lily – annoyed me, as I hold no love for bullies and fakers.<br /><br />Also, <strong>it’s all about the romance</strong>. Lily’s best friend only exists for Lily herself. The truth is, I don’t even remember her name. Strangely, I remember every name mentioned in this story but hers. If she was present, it was only to help Lily figure out some things. I don’t even know much about her. In Kasie West’s previous novels – for instance, <em>The Distance Between Us –</em> friendship had another meaning. A truer one.<br /><br />I’m glad for Lily’s big, loud family. They made me smile. And that darling rabbit, much love directed its way. The humour could also be diverting, though there wasn’t quite enough of it.<br /><br />I was pondering giving this a higher rating, as I know many of you will wish to throw your forks at me, but I can’t pretend – <strong>I’m very disappointed in <em>P.S. I Like You.</em></strong> The way I see it, even the title lacks originality.<br /><br />But I haven’t lost faith in Kasie West. I believe this isn’t the end of our reader-author relationship.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14557792666476747984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1274331384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1274331384" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1274331384?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=autobuy-authors">autobuy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=silly-fluff-but-hey-i-smiled">silly-fluff-but-hey-i-smiled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=in-a-minority-here">in-a-minority-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=arcs-2016">arcs-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1274331384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3477340922699376307"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467842454i/19637110._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>✨ AVAILABLE NOW ✨<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"If only there was a way to transport letters faster, through some sort of electronic device that codes messages and sends them through the air. But that’s just crazy talk."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Several times during my read I asked myself, <i>"what would it take for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25486998.P_S__I_Like_You' title='P.S. I Like You by Kasie West' rel='nofollow noopener'>P.S. I Like You</a> to reach a 4.5/5 stars?"</i> and in all honesty, I don't think it could, no matter how cute some parts were. Now, I'm all for rating a novel according to its genre, but where am I supposed to put <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West' title='Kasie West' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kasie West</a> books? In </span>
  <span id="freeText3477340922699376307" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467842454i/19637110._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✨ AVAILABLE NOW ✨<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"If only there was a way to transport letters faster, through some sort of electronic device that codes messages and sends them through the air. But that’s just crazy talk."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Several times during my read I asked myself, <i>"what would it take for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25486998.P_S__I_Like_You" title="P.S. I Like You by Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">P.S. I Like You</a> to reach a 4.5/5 stars?"</i> and in all honesty, I don't think it could, no matter how cute some parts were. Now, I'm all for rating a novel according to its genre, but where am I supposed to put <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West" title="Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">Kasie West</a> books? In YA contemporary? Sure! Then they can't - and will never - compete with the raw honesty and the avalanche of feelings I associate with some of my favorites : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellicoe Road</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6989576.Raw_Blue" title="Raw Blue by Kirsty Eagar" rel="nofollow noopener">Raw Blue</a>, to name a few. <br><br>Truth is, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25486998.P_S__I_Like_You" title="P.S. I Like You by Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">P.S. I Like You</a> put a smile on my face and was well, <i>cute</i>, but I cannot hide how unmemorable it is. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467842454i/19637111._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Fact #1</u>
</b> : I've read all of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West" title="Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">Kasie West</a>'s books and I've never come across a female lead like Lily, which is to say, the typical quirky girl with weird self-made clothes and notebooks. The tomboy, the popular girl, absolutely. Not the artist. <br><br><b>
  <u>Fact #2</u>
</b> : Yet I've read my fair share of YA novels, and <b>Lily doesn't bring anything different in the sea of female leads.</b> She likes music, makes (false) assumptions about people, is convinced that no guy would take an interest in her, fantasizes about this crooked-smiling, earbuds-addict guy with cool hair, has one and only friend because people suck (or something). When it comes to analyze someone else's actions, she's blind, but aren't we all? I mean, TEENAGER 101, anyone? I don't necessarily complain upfront about stereotypes, because sometimes they can be twisted to add something more to a story. Let's just say that <u>it wasn't the case in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25486998.P_S__I_Like_You" title="P.S. I Like You by Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">P.S. I Like You</a></u>. <br><br><b>
  <u>Fact #3</u>
</b> : <b>Lily's family is what I like the most about her, but it may be because it is so relatable to me</b>. A four children family and general messiness? It was my playground. Anyone who grew up in a family of six and who looks blank when confronted with the concept of a one child room will easily understand what she goes through. Her family is weird, crazy, annoying, roll-eyes worthy, yet so lovable, with a special award for Bugs Rabbit XD<br><br>As for the <b>love interest</b>, given the fact that it's supposed to be a "surprise" (come on, I knew who it was on page 6 - more on that later), I won't say his name but he was pretty great, if completely forgettable. I know, I know, I am harsh, but really : no matter how much he made me smile, mark my words : I will have forgotten his name next week. I just know it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467842454i/19637112._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Look, I'm all for pen pals and stuff, as it's a plot which usually really works for me. Yet if I accept having doubts, I still ask for the story <b>to keep its mystery</b>, at least a little. Take <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19547856.Simon_vs__the_Homo_Sapiens_Agenda" title="Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda by Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</a>, for example. I loved that I did not know if I was right until the very end. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25486998.P_S__I_Like_You" title="P.S. I Like You by Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">P.S. I Like You</a>, though? <b>I knew who her "mysterious" penpal was almost instantly, and every time a new event occurred, the threads were always so thick that I felt like I was only waiting for what I already knew to happen</b>. Granted, the story mostly revolved around Lily's romance with ***, and romance novels are always all kinds of predictable. Yet it annoyed me because given that I <i>knew</i> who it was, I couldn't help but feel the urge to skim through all the useless scenes with other boys. Just, nope. I didn't care, and it awfully felt like <b>filler</b> for me. <br><br>As for the <b>romance, I cannot deny that Lily and *** shared a great chemistry and that I rooted for them to get together</b> from the beginning. They made me smile, especially when they were writing to each other. But I cannot deny either that <b>something was missing</b>, or perhaps I'm finally too old for this kind of cute, kissing book. Maybe. See, it was adorable to see them getting to know each other, but it lacked some tension and character development in my opinion.<br><br>Finally, <b>the music part felt flat and contrived, and rather useless</b>. It's as if YA contemporaries <i>had</i> to incorporate some kind of artistic vibes, without needing them to add something to the story. I'm quite tired of this. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467842454i/19637113._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's no surprise that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West" title="Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">Kasie West</a>'s writing is <b>addictive and smile-inducing</b>. Her books, how flawed they can be, always manage to make me happy, even if my feelings stay superficial. However, if I really appreciated the letters, the dialogues didn't flow as well. Although they were often funny, <b>they sounded fake and I forced myself to adapt and ignore the stiffness - or rather, the fakeness</b>. Yes that's a thing.<br><br>► <b>All in all a cute but unmemorable novel.</b> I would still recommend it to anyone who needs to smile. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3477340922699376307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=ebook-format">ebook-format</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=galley-arc">galley-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=recommend-forever">recommend-forever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=stand-alone-books">stand-alone-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=can-t-frickin-wait">can-t-frickin-wait</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=scholastic">scholastic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1272779540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4159497184356947055">Can I ask a serious question? How does Kasie West do it… how does she manage to make me love each story she writes more than the last? I torture myself by reading them as soon as I can get my hands on them, which in turn makes me just have to wait even longer for the next, but I seriously can’t even help myself. <br/><br/>This book isn’t out until July of 2016… yes I said July 2016. That’s half a year away, and still, I didn’t even care. As soon as it was loaded onto my kindle app, I pull this beauty up a</span>
  <span id="freeText4159497184356947055" style="display:none">Can I ask a serious question? How does Kasie West do it… how does she manage to make me love each story she writes more than the last? I torture myself by reading them as soon as I can get my hands on them, which in turn makes me just have to wait even longer for the next, but I seriously can’t even help myself. <br /><br />This book isn’t out until July of 2016… yes I said July 2016. That’s half a year away, and still, I didn’t even care. As soon as it was loaded onto my kindle app, I pull this beauty up and dove in. <br /> <br />I mean… I love a lot of books. I just do. I’m an emotional reader so I tend to click with stories where I can relate to the characters and Kasie just manages to write the most realistic and fun characters around. <br /><br />Lily doesn’t fit in with the popular kids at school… she’s a bit quirky and definitely unique, focused less on the labels attached to her clothing and more on her creative side and trying to get her words to form a song or two. She’s a self-taught guitar player who dreams of writing music that means something to people, but in the meantime, she struggles through Chemistry and dealing with her overwhelming family. <br /><br />After writing one of her favorite bands lyrics on her desk in chemistry, she comes to class the next day only to find out that someone else in the school actually has good taste in music and has left her a message. One thing leads to another and she’s suddenly got a ‘pen pal’ in class that she ends up sharing more with than she does her best friend. As days and weeks pass, Lily finds herself wondering just who she might be clicking with. It’s not hard to figure out you guys… I mean there are quite a few indicators, and the summary isn’t stealthy about it at all but who the heck cares… it was so fun!! <br /> <br />Cade and Lily hate each other. Like HATE HATE each other. Their hate even came between Lily’s best friend’s relationship with Cade a couple years ago and culminated with a hated nickname he happened to give her that just happened to stick through the years.<br /><br />Cade is the complete opposite from Lily if everything is to be believed… perfect family, perfect house, perfect friends… but sometimes it’s easy to put up a front and as Lily learns who she’s connecting with via words and shared secrets she quickly finds that maybe Cade isn’t really the self-assured guy he shows everyone. <br /><br />I love Love / Hate relationship stories… the way the characters build that thin line that’s always present and gah… it’s just perfection. So after seeing the author name, the summary was next to catch my attention. Kasie always does an amazing job of building the connection between characters before having them ‘hook up’ in any way, and she does that really wonderfully here again. I absolutely love that these two are complete opposites in Every. Single. Way. Only to have them come together over words and thoughts … it was just lovely. <br /><br />I have to mention Lily’s family too, because they are a huge part of this story… no matter how messy or crazy or insane things were, it was so fun to see the traditions, to see them talk things out, to see them help each other… real live, wonderful families are so rare in YA that getting to see one is like Halley’s Comet- they only appear once every 75 years or so. (okay so I exaggerate a bit) <br /><br />It’s entirely possible that this might just be my favorite Kasie West book after reading, but then, I’ll probably change my mind once I reread her others … Is it okay to just say that I love them all equally and want to drown in her stories and words forever? <br /><br />If this one isn’t on your radar, put it there now! You’re going to absolutely love it when it arrives… in 7 months. OMG I’M SO SORRY FOR TEASING! I promise I’ll be waiting here with you because I’ll definitely be rereading this one as soon as it hits shelves! <br /><br />P.S. I like you Kasie... but you already know that :) <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4159497184356947055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2784358825683586638"><b>BEST. KASIE. BOOK. YET. ALL THE YESSSSES.</b> I have major book hangover now. I haven't had this bad of one in a long time. This book was SO. EFFING. GOOD.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469682111ra/19844020.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>THE TENSION, GUYS. THE TENSION:<br/><i>
  <blockquote>I can't make it stop.<br/>Please don't let it stop.<br/>You have me under your spell.<br/>If you knew me as well.<br/>You would make it stop.<br/>I can't let it stop.</blockquote>
</i><br/>Guys, I cheated. I told myself I was going to finish <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_' title='The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Raven Boys</a> first, but nope. I got an email alert that this precious coming out and I lasted, errr, a little over 24 </span>
  <span id="freeText2784358825683586638" style="display:none"><b>BEST. KASIE. BOOK. YET. ALL THE YESSSSES.</b> I have major book hangover now. I haven't had this bad of one in a long time. This book was SO. EFFING. GOOD.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469682111ra/19844020.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>THE TENSION, GUYS. THE TENSION:<br><i>
  <blockquote>I can't make it stop.<br>Please don't let it stop.<br>You have me under your spell.<br>If you knew me as well.<br>You would make it stop.<br>I can't let it stop.</blockquote>
</i><br>Guys, I cheated. I told myself I was going to finish <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17675462.The_Raven_Boys__The_Raven_Cycle___1_" title="The Raven Boys (The Raven Cycle, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">The Raven Boys</a> first, but nope. I got an email alert that this precious coming out and I lasted, errr, a little over 24 hours before I broke down and bought/read immediately.... And naturally I lost sleep and didn't stop for air until it was done.<br><br>I.am.not.joking.best.Kasie.book.yet. I am going through major withdrawals right now. This book Kasie gave me the trope I've been dying for her to use (the love-hate thing), and she added in a bonus one (anonymous letters, and who doesn't love the confusion and emotional turmoil that follows those). When I started it was easy to guess who would be the love interest the second he was introduced, just because if a character is mentioned a lot there is usually a reason. But yea, who cares if it's predictable? I was totally reading this baby for the tension, the beautiful TENSION that Kasie does oh-so-well. My only fault with her is that I always want more steamy moments and she keeps the romance very PG. But you know what? The tension is bloody divine so I forgive her.<br><blockquote>"--- couldn't be my pen pal.<br>He couldn't.<br>--- was an insensitive, selfish, arrogant jerk."</blockquote><br>&gt;&gt; (Seriously guys, you wondering why this is my favorite Kasie book, you know how much I adore love-hate stories)<br><blockquote>"So you think I'm hot."<br>"Doesn't every girl?"<br>It surprised me when his cheeks turned a light shade of pink. I wasn't sure why that embarrassed him in any way. I was positive he already knew it. He ran one hand through his hair. Then he said, almost too quiet for me to hear, "You're not every girl."</blockquote><br>My reaction every time a certain someone appeared on page (but really when you read you'll know, if you follow my reviews you will guess immediately because I have a very obvious "type" of love interest:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469682111ra/19844021.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>GAH. SO FREAKING GOOD. and I can't even write a halfway decent review because of all my rabid fangirlisms. And that flipping ending. The part where he reads her his part of letter when he confronts her. Dear, sweet lawd. Kasie seriously upped her game with this book guys. I expected this to be good, I mean, Kasie can't write a bad book, she just can't, but this was so much more. It beat out all her others for me. Go. Read it. It's worth it, and trust me, you want this book in your life. Quite possibly to make beautiful book babies with.</span>

It was so sweet and sometimes it's nice to read something sweet. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471660237ra/20087946.gif' alt=' ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Lily writes in her notebook at all times.   <span id="freeText10425360669655009331" style="display:none"><b>My August OwlCrate Box!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471551284i/20071800._SY540_.jpg" alt="My August OwlCrate Box!: " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I fell right in love with this book. After her teacher busts her she can't write in her notebook any more. Oh, the agony of trying to pay attention in chemistry. One day she writes some lyrics to her favorite band on the desk. It's really sweet because for the first time both of them can open up to another person and talk about their lives, which in some cases, are not that great. They never have enough money but they all love each other dearly. <br><br>I love how the relationship slowly becomes more between Lily and her secret penpal. <tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1273538589">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1939618466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1939618466" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1939618466?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1939618466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2904412426365769666">I bought this one for my daughter (<--target audience, btw) at a book fair and then decided to check it out for myself. Because I'm nosey.<br/>It was <i>cute</i>.<br/><br/>The gist is that there's this artsy girl who modifies thrift shop clothes, listens to indie rock bands, and doesn't realize that she's pretty. And like all artsy girls, she has a notebook filled with dreams, doodles, and lyrics she desperately wants to turn into a meaningful song - which she carries around with her all the time. She's unflinchingly</span>
  <span id="freeText2904412426365769666" style="display:none">I bought this one for my daughter (&lt;--target audience, btw) at a book fair and then decided to check it out for myself. Because I'm nosey.<br>It was <i>cute</i>.<br><br>The gist is that there's this artsy girl who modifies thrift shop clothes, listens to indie rock bands, and doesn't realize that she's pretty. And like all artsy girls, she has a notebook filled with dreams, doodles, and lyrics she desperately wants to turn into a meaningful song - which she carries around with her all the time. She's unflinchingly loyal to her one friend in the world because her artsiness and non-mainstream clothes keep all the normies from liking her.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526681851ra/25563960.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then you have the popular jock-boy who hides his secret pain with humor that is willfully misunderstood by the angsty indie girl and her guitar.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526681851ra/25563961.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>True <s>puppy</s> love ensues.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526681851ra/25563962.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And maybe it sounds like I didn't like this cliche riddled story, but that's not true! Started it last night, finished it this afternoon. This was exactly what was advertised and I quite enjoyed it. Formulas aren't necessarily a bad thing, especially when those formulas make you smile. This was the kind of adorable teenage fluff that I would gladly shove at my kids. And <i>I</i> definitely wouldn't mind grabbing more of this author's stuff for myself in the future, either.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2904412426365769666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1277298704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1277298704" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1277298704?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=in-the-minority-on-this-one">in-the-minority-on-this-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover">don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=not-released-yet">not-released-yet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need">physical-book-wishlist-want-it-need</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=arc-edelweiss">arc-edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1277298704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer382666505966989945"><br/><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> "So you think I'm hot?" <br/>"Doesn't every girl?"<br/>It surprised me when his cheeks turned a light shade of pink. I wasn't sure why that embarrassed him in any way. I was positive he already knew it. He ran one hand through his hair. Then he said, almost too quiet for me to hear, "You're not every girl." </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>I find it just so strange that I had never read a Kasie West novel until late last summer. Seriously-It’s so hard to find YA contemporary authors that make such a large range of</span>
  <span id="freeText382666505966989945" style="display:none"><br><b>*4.5 Stars*</b><br><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> "So you think I'm hot?" <br>"Doesn't every girl?"<br>It surprised me when his cheeks turned a light shade of pink. I wasn't sure why that embarrassed him in any way. I was positive he already knew it. He ran one hand through his hair. Then he said, almost too quiet for me to hear, "You're not every girl." </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I find it just so strange that I had never read a Kasie West novel until late last summer. Seriously-It’s so hard to find YA contemporary authors that make such a large range of people happy, that continue to produce cute, funny, witty, and memorable stories, and that <b>do it <i>well</i></b>. I had personally never heard of her, and then one of my best friends is like…are you <i>kidding</i>? Do you live under a rock?? READ HER NOW! So I picked up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15283043.The_Distance_Between_Us" title="The Distance Between Us by Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">The Distance Between Us</a> (Still my favorite Kasie West yet) and fell HARD. Who could resist Xander? Who I ask? WHO? <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>If only there was a way to transport letters faster, through some sort of electronic device that codes messages and sends them through the air. But that's just crazy talk.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>So here I am almost one year later, eagerly awaiting her next release. As soon as I ran out of her books (it was very quick lol) I was desperate for more. I can’t say she’s my absolute favorite author-that would be a lie-but what I <i>can</i> say is that <b>she is an author I have come to admire</b> and that I always look forward to reading. For instance, the minute this book was announced, I immediately had it on my TBR and let all of my friends know. And you can just tell how obsessed and loyal all her fans are. It’s so crazy! And the thing is…I truly <i>truly</i> had never heard of her. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/aa-1_zpsx6tciw7f.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467988362ra/19654062.gif" alt=" photo aa-1_zpsx6tciw7f.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But now I have, and what I’ve read is nothing but impressive. So here we are, sitting and anticipating her next release-<b>A cute little story about two students who both feel like they are missing something in their lives</b>…and seem to find and express themselves through the words of their favorite bands. What was meant to be just a release one day in chemistry for Lily becomes an instant connection between two people who are <b>desperate for someone to hear them</b>. It begins as a game, a playful flirtation that happens by chance in a boring chemistry class. But, as the days go by, it blossoms into something they look forward to and think about every single night long after the lights have gone out….and <b>turns into something far deeper</b> than they ever thought possible.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/2362-love-notes_zpsek9xkyfq.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467988362ra/19654063.gif" alt=" photo 2362-love-notes_zpsek9xkyfq.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I was both equally in love with this book and disappointed by it. And I know that sounds so crazy, what with my extremely high rating, but <b>I am so torn on this one</b>. On the one hand, I’ve seen this done before-and it was done WAY better. I’m sorry, I adore Kasie West, but that other novel is one of my favorites of all time and it had way more, I don’t know, heart. I’m not saying this wasn’t done well…but on the pen pal aspect, <b>I felt myself strangely detached</b>-and it wasn’t until I was done that I realized I wanted that same intensity I felt from my favorite and this didn’t get one tenth as deep as that. So, this aspect was an extreme let down for me-And I wasn’t even trying to compare. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Words brought us together though they almost kept us apart.<br>You trusted me with your secrets and then you stole my heart.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>And I’m sorry to be focusing on the negatives first, but I’d rather be salty and <i>then</i> sweet-I find it leaves a better taste in my mouth to <b>end on a happy, high note</b>. I had two other problems and one bothered me more than the other, if I’m being honest. I was a tad bored in the middle because the pen pal trope got a little bit stale, in my opinion. That's a small part of my disappointment. But, no, <b>my largest peeve</b>, and I’m sad to say this, <b>was the main character</b>.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/Writing-with-a-pencil-in-a-notebook-tumblr_m2mastM1zf1rqpem4o1_500_zpslt3qwhss.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467988362ra/19654064.gif" alt=" photo Writing-with-a-pencil-in-a-notebook-tumblr_m2mastM1zf1rqpem4o1_500_zpslt3qwhss.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I know, I <i>know</i>-I almost NEVER dislike the main girl, but for some reason I have been increasingly pickier with my female leads. Lily was…I liked Lily at first, ya know? But then I saw how judgmental she was…ON PURPOSE. She wasn’t simply just a snarky teenager, she <i>made</i> herself be that way. And <b>I didn’t realize until the final page just how deeply her attitude had affected me</b>. I adored how much she loved her family-it’s what my friend and I loved most about her. But then I saw how she reacted to said pen pal…it wasn’t enough that this person was a kindred spirit. It wasn’t enough that this person was <i>miserable</i> on the inside. It didn’t matter. <b>All she saw was what she wanted to see</b>, and even when said person proved they broke the mold of her pretentious expectations, she still pushed, fought, and clawed to keep things where it kept her comfortable. So she wanted to pigeonhole someone… but was indignant when she thought that others were doing the same to her. This really just…grr. This did NOT please me. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_m4f9o3GnnL1rpz875o1_500_large_zpsc2denaqh.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467988362ra/19654065.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_m4f9o3GnnL1rpz875o1_500_large_zpsc2denaqh.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And I told my friend this…That I just couldn’t get past her bias. And my friend Anna said-<i>‘Yeah, I get that. But teenagers are like that. They can be judgmental. I’m used to it.’</i> And it really bothered me long after-<b>Was I being too harsh</b>? And I finally decided...no, no I wasn’t. I love books where the heroines are unreasonable- I just couldn’t get past this one for whatever reason. <b>She bothered me</b>, plain and simple…and it was probably the largest reason I couldn’t fall head over heels for this story. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/nBJPU7L_zpszpsab12b.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467988362ra/19654066.gif" alt=" photo nBJPU7L_zpszpsab12b.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br> But enough of that. I have so many positive things to say about this. Like, how about the fact that after 50-60% I Could. Not. Put. This. Down. It became everything I’ve expected of a Kasie West novel and made me so badly wish that I’d had that connection from the very beginning. Imagine it like this:<br><br><b>Part one:</b> Cute introduction where the plot is set into play and we get to know all our quirky characters<br><br><b>Part two:</b> Pen pal plot drags a little, I begin to lose a little interest in Lily’s attitude and story<br><br><b>Part three:</b> TOTAL transformation where the plot finally expands and we truly connect to the pen pal and our main character (well...you know what I mean). This part was 100% a 5. Things ACTUALLY happen and it feels like an actual story with a flow and a final destination.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_n7r47abzM21s4wbdoo1_500_zps1qxxwn2m.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467988362ra/19654067.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_n7r47abzM21s4wbdoo1_500_zps1qxxwn2m.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And let me be clear-Had this whole story been like that last 40%, <b>this would have been my absolute favorite Kasie West book</b> (Probably). I just…I can’t explain how a complete lack of connection, focus, and butterflies turned into IMMEDIATE <b>butterflies that are so forceful</b> and so out of nowhere that <u>I couldn't breathe</u>. I’m not kidding. It’s like…okay, it’s like the Beast roller coaster at King’s Island (LOVE LOVE LOVE)-It’s a great coaster okay, but then you get to the final third of the coaster and there are all these wooden tunnels that make you go underground-ish and they are pitch black and you feel as if you are going 1000 times faster and, on the first turn into the first tunnel, your head whips to left so fast you can’t handle it-but you love it and it takes you completely by surprise as you laugh and scream and hold onto your partner for dear life. And, by the end, you have the biggest smile on your face and can't contain the good feels and your extreme excitement. <b>It was <i>just</i> like that</b>. Literally-Feels out of nowhere. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/couple-cute-grass-lain-down-Favim.com-671931_zpsbzwoqljs.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467988362i/19654068.png" alt=" photo couple-cute-grass-lain-down-Favim.com-671931_zpsbzwoqljs.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And I know I haven’t mentioned my main man WHO I AM OBSESSED WITH…but I don’t think I can because it’s a spoiler...is it, though? Is it not obvious? Okay, anyway, I can’t say his name, and I can’t really say much about him or it will make it even more obvious, and I can’t particularly claim he’s above Xander (maybe right below?), but <b>just know that I absolutely loved him</b>. He was an extremely kind, caring, and butterfly-inducing cutie. Misunderstood, if you will. But stop me now, I’m sure I’ve said too much. Whatever, sorry, it’s just <b>so damn hard for me not to say his name and gush and cry like a fangirl</b> professing her love and ah I am just a goner. But, alas, I guess you’ll have to meet him for yourself, unfortunately. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_n37sjjPOpt1t85f6vo1_500_zpsl2yqjsv1.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467988362ra/19654069.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_n37sjjPOpt1t85f6vo1_500_zpsl2yqjsv1.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So, anyway, it may seem like I was mostly down on this book...but that’s not the case. I just wanted people to understand why this isn’t a 5 when I’ve rated her others that way. <b>So many stories win me over in the end</b> (a million jump into my mind) and become a forever favorite and a five star. But when I struggled to love this story from the beginning and found that it paled in comparison to my lovelies, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18660447.The_Fill_In_Boyfriend" title="The Fill-In Boyfriend by Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fill-In Boyfriend</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15283043.The_Distance_Between_Us" title="The Distance Between Us by Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">The Distance Between Us</a>, <b>I can’t objectively and fairly give a five</b> for this story. I finished, was smiling so big it’s unreal, proclaimed my love of it to my friend, and said I had to give it a five…but then I slept on it and realized that it didn’t feel right to give it that rating, that it wasn’t a forever favorite, and it <b>it had too many issues I couldn't get over</b>. So, I decided to rate highly...because the amount of giddiness and happiness I felt for the final third of the story can’t be overlooked-but it didn’t surpass her other novels and needed to be rated thusly. This rating, while a little disheartening to me for KW, feels right and truly says what I want it to say: While this book had it’s issues, it was fun, addicting, butterfly-inducing, and brought the largest smile to my face. <b>P.S. is a good time, </b>if not a little forgettable, <b>and it will take you away from reality and make you feel better about yourself</b>. It will make you happier, if only for the length of the novel. And, really, what else can you ask for?<br><br><br><i>**ARC provided by Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review**</i><br><br><br><br><br>For more of my reviews, please visit:<br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="RSS" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/starcrossedbookblog/METU" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="BLOGLOVIN" href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/star-crossed-book-blog-13035961" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660579.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Google+" href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/b/116866754719786372049/+Starcrossedbookblog/posts" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439651670i/15866819.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>*********************<br><br>Alright guys...I'm guna be frank. My favorite thing about this book?? <b>AGHHHHH MY BOYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYYY</b>....he winssssss. Okay. Phew. Glad I got that out of the way. The boy was everything. He was the pitter-patter in my heart. The butterflies in my belly. <b>He was the smile on my face</b> and the driving force behind my high rating for this book. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/kijkhygtfr_zpsusdvumm0.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465222128ra/19327321.gif" alt="Spongebob photo kijkhygtfr_zpsusdvumm0.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Because, frankly? This wasn't my favorite Kasie West novel. And I couldn't quite put my finger on why until this morning:<br><br>Spoiler alert?<br><br><u>I hated the MC. </u><br><br>Sorry not sorry.<br><br>RTC.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer10889519686262145789">4.5/5 stars<br/><br/>This book contains my least favorite trope but it's done SO WELL and with just enough to counter balance it that I loved it?? Was not expecting that. I really REALLY REALLY liked this book for a lot of reasons. The characters were fantastic, especially the main character. I loved the romance in this book because it wasn't insta-love. It took a bit to develop and come about, and even then it still took a little longer. LOVE ME SOME (kind of) SLOW BURN. The whole plot and premise are so</span>
  <span id="freeText10889519686262145789" style="display:none">4.5/5 stars<br /><br />This book contains my least favorite trope but it's done SO WELL and with just enough to counter balance it that I loved it?? Was not expecting that. I really REALLY REALLY liked this book for a lot of reasons. The characters were fantastic, especially the main character. I loved the romance in this book because it wasn't insta-love. It took a bit to develop and come about, and even then it still took a little longer. LOVE ME SOME (kind of) SLOW BURN. The whole plot and premise are so fun and really intriguing from the start, it's the perfect mix of a lot of different elements.<br />The things I didn't like were the pacing of the ending (everything seemed to move a little too fast) and I would've loved a *touch* more development for the side characters, though it's hard to do in a book this short. It's not to say that they weren't well developed, but I think it could've been done a little more.<br />Overall a SUPER fun contemporary that I really enjoyed and read in essentially one plane ride. I could NOT put it down! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4814780826213746172">I like my books <i>cheesy and cute and fluffy</i> sometimes and this was just the perfect one. I am honestly so <b>pleasantly surprised</b> right now and I just need a moment to gather all my feels. <br/><a href='https://gifyu.com/image/bqAj' rel='nofollow noopener'>

Kind of like You’ve Got Mail I guess (which makes me love it even more). SO Lily starts writing on her desk one day because she’s bored durin</span>
  <span id="freeText4814780826213746172" style="display:none">I like my books <i>cheesy and cute and fluffy</i> sometimes and this was just the perfect one. I am honestly so <b>pleasantly surprised</b> right now and I just need a moment to gather all my feels. <br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/bqAj" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496588961ra/22930897.gif" alt="gay-feels-gif.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>ALSO its official</b>: I love Kasie West’s writings&amp; I’m ready to read <i>everything and anything</i> by her<br>The plot obviously pulled me in first. The whole premise is so adorable. Kind of like You’ve Got Mail I guess (which makes me love it even more). SO Lily starts writing on her desk one day because she’s bored during Chemistry (relatable btw) and someone answers back. And the whole concept was so sweet. The way Lily managed to get to know you-know-who was so adorable.<br>The family aspects and friendship was beautiful and I really want more Kasie West right now. <br><br>OK BUT the characters firstly were so amazing let me just cry here.<br><b>Lily</b><br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/bqAF" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496588961ra/22930896.gif" alt="3109739933_1_3_2Riry1QH.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I love her character so much. She was funny, witty and just a ton of fun to follow. Also her love for music played a huge role in her character and it was so refreshing and sweet to follow. Her love for music and being inside her brain as she looked for inspiration for her songs and finally gained courage to show it to the world was so much fun. Her relationships with her family is honestly the best and it was so fun to see her interact with her little brothers (who are the sweetest things every okay). <br><b>Cade</b><br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/bqAa" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496588961ra/22930895.gif" alt="originalbe97b.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>I LOVE THIS GUY.</b> Honestly I don’t know what to really say about Cade except that he’s adorable and cliché but I don’t care okay he is perfect. He was so sweet and supportive and I can’t say anything except that I love him. A lot. <br><i>Honestly I’m kind of a mess and from here so it’s just going to get messy and I’m just going to list all the stuff in this book I loved:</i><br>a)	The “evil rabbit” named bugs rabbit which likes to pee on unsuspecting people<br>b)	The adorable brothers of Lily who are so cute ohmy <br>c)	Ashley (her sister) and Lily’s relationship #goals<br>d)	Lily’s entire family and how messy and real they are<br>e)	How competitive Lily’s parents are because LOL same<br>f)	The whole note exchanging thing is so pure <br>g)	The fact that Lily and you-know-who bond through music<br>h)	Lily&amp; her best friend’s relationship<br>i)	The fact that you-know-who likes kids and is so good to Wyatt<br>j)	THAT ENDING <br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/giphy_zps731abhki.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472295531ra/20176800.gif" alt=" photo giphy_zps731abhki.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Look guys if you just want to feel all them feels this is the book for it okay. It’s so cute and it will definitely lift you off a slump.<br></span>

<div id="review_1943937286" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1943937286" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1943937286?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1943937286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9945576375103315102"><b>UPDATED REVIEW</b><br/><br/>SSSSSWWWWOOONN!!I That was all sorts of adorable. I can’t even. I think this is officially my favorite <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54160269.I_smile_at_him__and_take_just_one_more_stolen_step__until_were_five_feet_apart_The_Fault_in_our_Stars_meets_Kasie_West_in_this_beautiful______with_the_emotional_maturity_of_adults' title='I smile at him ,and take just one more stolen step, until were five feet apart The Fault in our Stars meets Kasie West in this beautiful, ... with the emotional maturity of adults by Rachael Lippincott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kasie West</a> novel and I’m so glad that I decided to reread this, gladder that it was so much better than the first time I read it. I can’t believe how I easily wrote this off the first time as some clichéd romantic comedy because this was quite very well written and despite the familiar elements, letter writing, anonymity and stuff, it came off quite very original. <br/><br/>It also helps a </span>
  <span id="freeText9945576375103315102" style="display:none"><b>UPDATED REVIEW</b><br /><br />SSSSSWWWWOOONN!!I That was all sorts of adorable. I can’t even. I think this is officially my favorite <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54160269.I_smile_at_him__and_take_just_one_more_stolen_step__until_were_five_feet_apart_The_Fault_in_our_Stars_meets_Kasie_West_in_this_beautiful______with_the_emotional_maturity_of_adults" title="I smile at him ,and take just one more stolen step, until were five feet apart The Fault in our Stars meets Kasie West in this beautiful, ... with the emotional maturity of adults by Rachael Lippincott" rel="nofollow noopener">Kasie West</a> novel and I’m so glad that I decided to reread this, gladder that it was so much better than the first time I read it. I can’t believe how I easily wrote this off the first time as some clichéd romantic comedy because this was quite very well written and despite the familiar elements, letter writing, anonymity and stuff, it came off quite very original. <br /><br />It also helps a lot how closely I could relate with <b>Lily</b> - always and awkward and self-deprecatingly funny. <br /><br /><b> <i> “You thought my awkwardness was from preconceived plans to be awkward?”<br /><br />“Yeah, that’s me, the girl whose social life makes everyone feel better about theirs.” </i></b>  <br /><br />I also love the part where she loves to write song lyrics and actually plays the guitar while also designing unusual but really cool outfits. Her family is the best and there so many moments in their home that simply warmed my heart like I could practically picture visiting the Abbott’s home myself, picking which is the better pie or necklace (the one by her dad or her mom?), meeting her siblings especially the “Things” (Wyatt and Jonah) and even taking a peek on Bugs Rabbit’s’ cage especially the special one Lily’s dad designed. <br /><br />Lily’s friendship with <b>Isabel</b> is perfect. I love their honesty and loyalty with each other, how they always watched each other’s backs and how much understanding they have for each other. It’s really the best. <br /><br />Best of all, the romance! The anonymous letter writing is amazing. It’s mysterious, adventurous, really funny and it gave a glimpse to who the main characters are really including the parts of themselves they try to hide from others. The connection between Lily and this super cute guy (I wouldn’t mention his name for the benefit of those who haven’t read this yet) is truly adorbs. I kept swooning and never rolled my eyes, not even once and that, I believe, merits five shining stars! LoL! <br /><br /><br /><br />***ORIGINAL REVIEW***<br /><br /><b>3.5 stars </b><br /><br />I honestly didn’t think I’ll end up liking the novel because the first few chapters didn’t do much for me. I wasn’t instantly captivated and I wasn’t that eager to keep reading during the first few chapters. But then came the letter exchanges and I was in. The main characters’ true personalities shone through their words and I eventually fell for both of them. Also, who am I kidding? It’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West" title="Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">Kasie West</a>, instantly garnering the novel half a star. <br /><br />But as much as I liked the novel, I honestly don’t think a Kasie West book deserves five stars because they’re consistently predictable, clichéd, fluffy, sometimes too fluffy but to me, they’re the perfect laid-back reads you can bring with you while are on a vacation which I was and I totally enjoyed it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9945576375103315102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText310343480384187718" style="display:none">Of course it was perfect, it's Kasie. <br /><br />I legit shoved a friend out of the way when I saw this gorgeous thing on the shelf at my local indie, so of course I was going to read it ASAP.<br /><br />Lily is a great MC. I loved how much she loves music and writing lyrics. Her family was fun {all of those contests and voting had me cackling} and her little brothers were adorable.<br /><br />I love love love the idea of secret pen pals and letters and this was just perfection. Kasie threw in a couple of mild twists I wasn't expecting, but had me grinning like a loon the entire time. Obviously I would have wanted more, because I always do, but the ending was sweet and just what I wanted. </span>

<div id="review_1273109887" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1273109887" />
    <a title="Sophie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie"><img alt="Sophie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564510350p2/8563233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1273109887?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie" href="/user/show/8563233-sophie">Sophie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781407188072" href="/book/show/39874309-ps-i-like-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=own-read">own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=2017-contemporary-romance-challenge">2017-contemporary-romance-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1273109887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13218811033462933682">I have adored Kasie West's books since I read one for the very first time. Every time she brings out a new book, I'm immediately intrigued, and with this book, that was no different. The premise was unlike any book I've read before, and because of Kasie's style, I was hooked from the first page.<br/><br/>The main character, Lily, is bored during chem class - like many students to come before her. When her teacher restricts her paper to one sheet, so that she makes only chemistry notes, and nothing else. T</span>
  <span id="freeText13218811033462933682" style="display:none">I have adored Kasie West's books since I read one for the very first time. Every time she brings out a new book, I'm immediately intrigued, and with this book, that was no different. The premise was unlike any book I've read before, and because of Kasie's style, I was hooked from the first page.<br /><br />The main character, Lily, is bored during chem class - like many students to come before her. When her teacher restricts her paper to one sheet, so that she makes only chemistry notes, and nothing else. To deal with this, she ends up writing the lyrics of her favourite song on the desk, and is surprised that the lyrics are finished by someone else, next time she's in that class. Somehow, she's made a pen pal, and when the notes become lengthier, and more personal, she finds herself falling for the person on the other side of the sheet.<br /><br />I loved how Kasie dropped in hints here and there to point the way to the mystery 'pen pal'. We learnt who it was as Lily did, and I was very happy with the reveal. Unlike many other books, we didn't have to wait until the end of the book to find out; rather, Lily learnt who her pen pal was about half way through the book, though it took a while until both revealed themselves to each other. Because of this wait, and Lily knowing who it was she was falling for, and still falling harder, it made the book so much better to read.<br /><br />Like you'll have guessed, the romance was so swoony! I sped through this book in a few hours, and had a grin on my face the entire time. Lily and her love interest had the best chemistry, and once they had the big reveal, the chemistry grew - and no, that's not a pun. Kasie gets better with every single book, and I think this is my favourite so far. I'm looking forward to getting my hands on By Your Side, and other future books by Kasie.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13218811033462933682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1788623693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1788623693" />
    <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is"><img alt="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516737798p2/4467515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1788623693?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is">Jasmine from How Useful It Is</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
